    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer8045875786441615490"><b>The Prize-Winning Cult Classic and International Bestseller with Over 1 Million Copies Sold</b> <br/><br/> Describing a world as amoral and fascinating as the landscapes of <i>Less Than Zero</i> and <i>Trainspotting</i>, this novel about a young woman living in the violent world of Japan's underground youth culture is both shocking and strangely beautiful. <p> Enchanted by the snakelike forked tongue of</p></span>
  <span id="freeText8045875786441615490" style="display:none"><b>The Prize-Winning Cult Classic and International Bestseller with Over 1 Million Copies Sold</b> <br /><br /> Describing a world as amoral and fascinating as the landscapes of <i>Less Than Zero</i> and <i>Trainspotting</i>, this novel about a young woman living in the violent world of Japan's underground youth culture is both shocking and strangely beautiful. <p> Enchanted by the snakelike forked tongue of a stranger called Ama, nineteen-year-old Lui takes a walk on another side of life. Following Ama home the night she meets him, Lui straightaway moves in with him and begins making plans to have her own tongue pierced. Determined to push her boundaries further, she asks Ama's strange friend Shiba to design an exquisite dragon tattoo for her back. But when Lui and Shiba begin an affair, Ama's jealousy is stirred and the situation becomes explosive.</p></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_14197989" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14197989" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65207-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465962504p2/65207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14197989?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/65207-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one, even people i dislike </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65207-shannon?shelf=festival-of-suck">festival-of-suck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer14197989&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14197989" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3635976262437994913">Edit: I should mention that this is the only book I have ever hated so much that I actually <i>threw it away</i>. I refuse to even like, give it to the used bookstore, because I don't want anyone else to have to read it. <br/><br/>I HATE THIS BOOK.<br/><br/>My first thought when I began reading this was "This is incredibly, unbelievably poorly written". The feeling did not go away. This book is translated from Japanese. The translator should be fired. Though it is entirely possible that the translation is sufficient and t</span>
  <span id="freeText3635976262437994913" style="display:none">Edit: I should mention that this is the only book I have ever hated so much that I actually <i>threw it away</i>. I refuse to even like, give it to the used bookstore, because I don't want anyone else to have to read it. <br /><br />I HATE THIS BOOK.<br /><br />My first thought when I began reading this was "This is incredibly, unbelievably poorly written". The feeling did not go away. This book is translated from Japanese. The translator should be fired. Though it is entirely possible that the translation is sufficient and the book is just really fucking horrible. Which is what I expect is the case. The characters are SO badly and inconsistently portrayed, the plot is ridiculous; it relies entirely on "shocking" events, because there is no substance behind the story. There is seriously nothing redeemable about this book. Not one line. AAGH SERIOUSLY. ITS CAPLOCK TIME. STOP TRYING SO FUCKING HARD TO BE EDGY, BOOK. OHHH LOOK AT ME, I'M GOING TO FORK MY TONGUE AND HAVE SOME DOUCHEBAG TATTOO ME, AND INSTEAD OF PAYMENT I'LL JUST LET HIM BANG ME BECAUSE I'M A GIANT BORING ANOREXIC WHORE. THIS IS SUCH A FUCKING EDGY STORY INST IT?<br /><br />I am going to summarize the plot (because apparently i'm a sadist) so.. warning: SPOILERS. Not that it matters.<br /><br />There is this unaffected, vapid, stupid 19 year old girl(you don't know really anything about her, her past or anything, only the way she reacts to the stupid men in this book, from which I was forced to deduce that she's a moron), and she starts going out with this guy because he has a forked tongue, or something. Then she decides to get a forked tongue, so she gets it pierced to start the process. Enter crazy asshole piercer guy: he's a friend of her forked tongue boyfriend guy and he's A COMPLETE DOUCHEBAG IN EVERY WAY. They are hanging out and then randomly some guy hits on stupid girl and her boyfriend KILLS HIM, PULLS OUT HIS TEETH, AND GIVES THEM TO THE GIRL. They flee from the scene. Then a lot of boring shit happens, the girl wants a tattoo, she keeps stretching the jesus out of her tongue, blahblah. THEN OH MY GOODNESS she realizes the police are after her forked-tongue quasi-boyfriend guy, because apparently even ridiculously trendy 18 year olds aren't allowed to murder people. She, being a genius, has him change his hair color. Then suddenly he goes missing. And (PLOT TWIST) he is killed. And then she and piercer guy get a call from the mortuary to identify his body. It is revealed that before he was killed he was raped and tortured mercilessly. She is sad about this and she goes anorexic, because anorexia is so awesomely cool and edgy, I suspect. She bangs the piercer guy some more. Then she puts together a few obvious pieces that SUDDENLY appear conveniently (nice plot development) and realizes that is it extremely likely that the crazy piercer guy was the one who killed and raped forked tongue guy. She bangs the piercer guy some more, because I guess, who cares that he raped and killed that other guy, I mean, whatever, life sucks and the main girl is SUCH A FUCKING MYSTERIOUS EDGY CHICK OR WHATEVER. <b>THE END.</b><br /><br />Basically, this may be THE worst book I've ever read, but it's hard to say. I'm angry about this. Not because it's a shitty book and I purchased it and read it, but because IT HAD FUCKING RAVE REVIEWS all over it. I mean, one of the back was from Marie Claire (some stupid magazine) and it was like "edgy and sexy and on top of that, well written" (or something).. and that's easy to brush aside because, I mean, what the fuck do the writers at Marie Clair magazine know about literature anyway? But on the front of this fucking thing, from the fucking New York Times, it just says "powerful". WHAT. Did they just edit this? Was the review just "powerful...y fucking useless"? Because if not, screw you, New York Times. THIS BOOK ALSO WON SOME KIND OF PRIZE. AND IS AN INTERNATIONAL BEST-SELLER. OVER 1 MILLION COPIES SOLD WHAT? THIS BLOWS MY MIND. So, to the people among those 1 million who bought this book and liked it: screw you, you have unforgivably horrible taste.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3635976262437994913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122371323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122371323" />
    <a title="Caro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3927155-caro"><img alt="Caro" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122371323?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caro" href="/user/show/3927155-caro">Caro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3927155-caro?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3927155-caro?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3927155-caro?shelf=foreign-literature">foreign-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122371323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6846045379894562243">I was introduced to Hitomi Kanehara at an author event with Melvin Burgess. He talked about several YA books by Japanese authors who didn't try to write about adults in teenage disguise but about real teenagers. I was very intrigued and bought the tiny book that is Snakes and Earrings. My friend Sabrina and I read it and we just couldn't stop thinking and talking about this book.<br/><br/><br/>The book has extremely explicit content and I will mention that content in my review, so if you are faint-hearted, ple</span>
  <span id="freeText6846045379894562243" style="display:none">I was introduced to Hitomi Kanehara at an author event with Melvin Burgess. He talked about several YA books by Japanese authors who didn't try to write about adults in teenage disguise but about real teenagers. I was very intrigued and bought the tiny book that is Snakes and Earrings. My friend Sabrina and I read it and we just couldn't stop thinking and talking about this book.<br /><br /><br />The book has extremely explicit content and I will mention that content in my review, so if you are faint-hearted, please, do not read any further. (I'm talking about tattoos, piercings, sex, alcohol, drugs, self mutilation)<br /><br />Lui, self destruction and depression<br />As my friend pointed out, Lui is possibly suffering from depression. half of the time she feels numb and the other she abuses her body in all possible way, in an attempt to feel something. But the book is extremely surprising and what you feel will happen to Lui doesn't really happen.<br />You never know if you have to blame Lui for what happens or pity her, and I felt that the book wasn't exactly about this. It is a glimpse into this girl's self destructive circle. She stays with Ama and you can see he has so many feelings for her that she is incapable to share or reciprocate. <br />Lui is also a masochist, she enjoys being hurt in sexual relations. I would link this to the fact that she has no respect for her body, but anyone could have these tastes. It is undeniably creepy to read some of the scenes, but it is interesting to see how Lui conceives it in her head. <br /><br />Counter-culture in Japan<br />The depiction of counter-culture in Japan is simply mesmerizing. This is why I love reading translated books from foreign countries, you learn so much! I had no idea that groups like "Barbie girls" and "punks" were so distinctive in Japan. <br />It is also always very interesting to read about people living on the fringe. Our lives are so organised and ruled by social conventions that sometimes we might forget who we are. People living on the fringe don't have this need to abide by the rules and are, in a way, much more natural than we are.<br />The book also shows a new generation. If earlier generations were rebellious or ambitious, we are, if anything, a bored generation. Nothing surprises us or moves us. We have even stopped dreaming. We live in a state of suspension from which nothing can shake us except fake emotions and convictions. When I read about Lui's story, I saw that in her. <br /><br />Tattoos and piercing<br />To which extent are they a form of art? This is an endless question and there isn't one answer. As a fan of the form of art, I would agree with Shiba's vision of them. They are a way to magnify the body, not change it. Whereas Lui doesn't have any respect or consideration for her body. The book is an interesting way to explore this theme and see the two visions. By experience, not two tattoo artist or tattooed person have the same conception of what a tattoo or a piercing is. As widespread as the practice might be, it is a very personal experience.<br />Lui is first attracted to Ama because she is fascinated by his forked tongue. She decides to do this to herself (the process includes to get your tongue pierced and then to stretch the hole progressively). She also wants a unique tattoo and asks Shiba to design it. The descriptions are completely realistic and people not familiar with them might be a little put off. <br /><br />The style of the book<br />I feel that this book wants to depict reality as it is and not create a false image of teenagers with a conscience or with any sense of responsability. I find the style haunting. This story creeps on you and you find yourself vehemently disliking Lui for what she does to herself and others. But she grows on you at some point.<br /><br /><br />This is a masterpiece of a book. It is short but will give you a sense of whole which only a 700+ pages book can do. It is simply marvelous and an incredible way to make you discover another culture, another way of life, and yourself - maybe - in the process.<br /><br />It may be a Young Adult book but obviously not for our standards since it was published as an adult book in the UK and has so much explicit content I cannot even begin to enumerate it. So consider yourself informed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6846045379894562243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3443988536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7406717818727100773">Unlike Ryu Murakami's transgressive works, this small book lacks polish. It deals with the immature, shallow concerns of its adolescent characters with stark, unapologetic realism. Edgy in the extreme, but lacking depth of any appreciable kind, it reads quickly and has all of the trappings of a bestselling Japanese alternative pop literary prize winner. It is a shame that the Akutagawa Prize is handed out to such amateurish attention-grabbing authors, which make their way into English, but canno</span>
  <span id="freeText7406717818727100773" style="display:none">Unlike Ryu Murakami's transgressive works, this small book lacks polish. It deals with the immature, shallow concerns of its adolescent characters with stark, unapologetic realism. Edgy in the extreme, but lacking depth of any appreciable kind, it reads quickly and has all of the trappings of a bestselling Japanese alternative pop literary prize winner. It is a shame that the Akutagawa Prize is handed out to such amateurish attention-grabbing authors, which make their way into English, but cannot compete with even the common run of American rebellious teen novels.</span>

<div id="review_5556575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5556575" />
    <a title="Michaela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76700-michaela"><img alt="Michaela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535998825p2/76700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5556575?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michaela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michaela" href="/user/show/76700-michaela">Michaela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525948896" href="/book/show/922712.Snakes_and_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5556575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4173631591520777117">This book made me feel like I was in workshop again and reading the first draft of someone's manuscript. I don't know if something got lost in translation, but the writing isn't sophisticated -- it seems really amateurish. (And yes, I realize this is first novel, but the writing still bothers me. Everything is overwritten, and there are a lot of cliches.) The dialogue is choppy in a bad way. (I really hate it when people tag their dialogue with adverbs because the actual dialogue itself/context </span>
  <span id="freeText4173631591520777117" style="display:none">This book made me feel like I was in workshop again and reading the first draft of someone's manuscript. I don't know if something got lost in translation, but the writing isn't sophisticated -- it seems really amateurish. (And yes, I realize this is first novel, but the writing still bothers me. Everything is overwritten, and there are a lot of cliches.) The dialogue is choppy in a bad way. (I really hate it when people tag their dialogue with adverbs because the actual dialogue itself/context that it's in should convey how the words are said, thereby making the use of adverbs totally unnecessary.) Also, I feel like some of the body-piercing stuff is wrong. For example, has anyone ever heard of anyone getting their tongue pierced with a piercing gun?? I haven't -- and I had my tongue pierced for six years. As far as I know, piercers use a needle, not a gun. (Who knows -- maybe they do it differently in Japan.) I've also never heard of anyone saying that the tongue is the most painful part of the body to get pierced. Everyone I know who's gotten their tongue pierced (including myself) didn't think it hurt much at all. (I immediately went home and ate mashed potatoes after my piercing -- no problem.) Since piercing is such a major theme in this book, you'd think this stuff should at least be accurate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4173631591520777117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_430697502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430697502" />
    <a title="Jim Elkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13493599-jim-elkins"><img alt="Jim Elkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349748317p2/13493599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430697502?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Elkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Elkins" href="/user/show/13493599-jim-elkins">Jim Elkins</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13493599-jim-elkins?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430697502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7183478290638994615">The speed of some Japanese fiction from the 1990s and 2000s <br/><br/>There is an odd quality in some Japanese fiction about nihilistic, suicidal, or otherwise desperate teenagers: it is written so fast that even the most desolate scenes are easy to read. Compare A.L. Kennedy to this! The incidents and the lives in this book are potentially interesting, but the prose runs so quickly and carelessly that the book is forgettable.<br/><br/>The speed of Japanese fiction was noted in the spring 2008 issue of "Calque," an</span>
  <span id="freeText7183478290638994615" style="display:none">The speed of some Japanese fiction from the 1990s and 2000s <br /><br />There is an odd quality in some Japanese fiction about nihilistic, suicidal, or otherwise desperate teenagers: it is written so fast that even the most desolate scenes are easy to read. Compare A.L. Kennedy to this! The incidents and the lives in this book are potentially interesting, but the prose runs so quickly and carelessly that the book is forgettable.<br /><br />The speed of Japanese fiction was noted in the spring 2008 issue of "Calque," an excellent magazine of translations. Michael Emmerich, writing about Matsuura Rieko, says her output of 6 books of fiction is "astonishing" because it's so small. The author Kakuta Mitsuyo, he says, publishes six books every year. I wonder if the conventions of some Japanese fiction run counter to some of the subject matter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7183478290638994615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14527236765107301057">Short, extremely well written (and translated obviously) and very compelling in a way a train wreck is; describing an amoral brutal world of young Tokyo underground, where casual violence, drinking, body mods from the milder to the extreme and a day to day approach to life that leads nowhere, I can see why it won the prestigious Akutagawa prize and sold 1 million plus copies in Japan as well as being translated and reviewed in the English speaking world so well<br/><br/>not for the squeamish, though not a</span>
  <span id="freeText14527236765107301057" style="display:none">Short, extremely well written (and translated obviously) and very compelling in a way a train wreck is; describing an amoral brutal world of young Tokyo underground, where casual violence, drinking, body mods from the milder to the extreme and a day to day approach to life that leads nowhere, I can see why it won the prestigious Akutagawa prize and sold 1 million plus copies in Japan as well as being translated and reviewed in the English speaking world so well<br /><br />not for the squeamish, though not as brutal or explicit as it could have been (it still is but I read worse/more), while the violence and darkness is mostly of the immediate, visceral kind which is clearly on the voyeuristic side for readers of books (as the main heroine Lui puts it, she only reads a tabloid where she gets all her info), rather than the psychological darkness and struggles of the more intellectual kind <br /><br />definitely recommended if in the mood for something like this (the blurb is fairly accurate and the novel is really very short with three main characters and a world that is both immediate/actual and distant/unreal to them)<br /><br /> and for the people who like such, there is a movie adaptation with the same title from 2008 (youtube has both a trailer and parts of it, generally translated) which seems to be very accurately following the novel from what i saw, so you can get a visual feel for the book too</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14700286032325640492">........................<br/>I read this because Namjoon suggested it; almost gave up five pages into the book but I finished it anyway, glad I did. <br/>The story is of a young girl who finds a guy fascinating because of his body modification and ends up moving in with him pretty much immediately. He takes her to his friends tattoo parlour, to do the same modification, and she ends up having an ‘affair’ with tattoo guy. What I liked was the development of her character, even though it was just over a 100</span>
  <span id="freeText14700286032325640492" style="display:none">........................<br />I read this because Namjoon suggested it; almost gave up five pages into the book but I finished it anyway, glad I did. <br />The story is of a young girl who finds a guy fascinating because of his body modification and ends up moving in with him pretty much immediately. He takes her to his friends tattoo parlour, to do the same modification, and she ends up having an ‘affair’ with tattoo guy. What I liked was the development of her character, even though it was just over a 100 pages you could really see her progress- in thoughts, in actions. <br />It was a SMIDGE too graphic for me (pls note sarcasm, the characters were all teenagers and that bugged me to no end that they were doing shit like this), but it was an interesting read I must say.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14700286032325640492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_222406252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222406252" />
    <a title="Lakis Fourouklas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6312888-lakis-fourouklas"><img alt="Lakis Fourouklas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442616092p2/6312888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222406252?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lakis Fourouklas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lakis Fourouklas" href="/user/show/6312888-lakis-fourouklas">Lakis Fourouklas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099483670" href="/book/show/922711.Snakes_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222406252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4120323607083388282">Snakes and Earrings is not a book for the tenderhearted; even though it does become tender every now and then. Actually this is a very harsh story, talking about a hard world; the world of Lui, Ama and Shiba-san. It’s a story about a different way of life; a way of life that breaths and breeds in the darkness of the human soul; of life without hope.<br/> The three heroes live inside this world of ours, but mostly at the side of it. They know everything about its conventions, but they do not abide to </span>
  <span id="freeText4120323607083388282" style="display:none">Snakes and Earrings is not a book for the tenderhearted; even though it does become tender every now and then. Actually this is a very harsh story, talking about a hard world; the world of Lui, Ama and Shiba-san. It’s a story about a different way of life; a way of life that breaths and breeds in the darkness of the human soul; of life without hope.<br /> The three heroes live inside this world of ours, but mostly at the side of it. They know everything about its conventions, but they do not abide to them. They are just themselves and the road to destruction is paved by their own hand.<br /> It all begins when Lui, a kind of a Barbie girl with as many earrings as one can get, meets Ama, a total freak who has even more piercings on his body than her. They hit it off right away and before too long she moves in with him. What did she find so attractive about him? What else did you expect but his forked-tongue and his tattoos? She’s mystified by this creature. And she feels jealous. She needs a tongue just like his. But not only that; she also wishes to have engraved on her body the most original tattoo anyone ever made. It’s exactly because of her dark wishes that she finds her way, along with Ama, into the workshop of Shiba-san, a real master in the arts of piercing and tattooing. As she walks through that door, the floodgates of hell seem to open wide and the oncoming waters are bound to rush her into the abyss.<br /> Lui is an extreme character. She likes falling down psychologically time and again; to dive in with no regrets into the worlds of sin; to torment her body without giving it a second thought. She seems to live in order to suffer, and it’s exactly this pain that keeps her alive. She may be an item with Ama but she doesn’t hesitate to sleep with Shiba-san; even after he says that he really wants to kill her. At the same time she feels almost ecstatic at the idea of her forked-tongue. Actually she’s so eager to get it that she places herself into a spot of insurmountable pain; almost flirting with insanity. Ama, despite his looks, is quite a sensitive man and he really loves Lui. He hates watching her doing bad things to herself but doesn’t seem to have the power to stop her. He’d even kill for her; if she didn’t kill herself first that is. As for Shiba-san, well, he’s a man without a trace of humanity in him. He likes inflicting pain and that’s probably why he’s doing what he’s doing for a living. However, maybe, just maybe, he’s not completely lost, and a tragic event is all that it will take to bring some samples of goodness out of his dark heart and into the light.<br /> Snakes and Earrings is mainly a book of characters. The plot is not so important. The author doesn’t treat her creations with a gentle hand by with extreme harshness. She has a story to tell, and she’ll stop at nothing, in order to do so. The modern Japanese society comes under the microscope, goes through her fine filter and comes out at the other side just as bad as it could ever be. Sex, violence, drugs, alcohol, prostitution, fears; she talks about all these matters in a masterful way, in a raw language that could be hard to cope with, but which is the only one that could describe things as they really are.<br /> This is a hell of a novel, about the hell of some people’s everyday lives.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4120323607083388282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64742778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64742778" />
    <a title="Evan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1248986-evan"><img alt="Evan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488574589p2/1248986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64742778?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan" href="/user/show/1248986-evan">Evan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525948896" href="/book/show/922712.Snakes_and_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=__in-my-collection">__in-my-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=sexuality">sexuality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=2009-reads">2009-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1248986-evan?shelf=japonais">japonais</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64742778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1497763976943702092">He who speak with forked tongue...may not necessarily be wise (or some such)...<br/>Fairly simple tome. Japanese urban youth culture. Barbie girl goes to techno club and meets bad boy with a forked snake tongue obtained through gradual body modification/mutilation (take your pick). She becomes fascinated and turned on, they fuck immediately; she becomes immersed in the tattoo and piercing/ body modification world; wants a snake tongue, too, yadda yadda. Kind of fascinating so far as a socio-cultural </span>
  <span id="freeText1497763976943702092" style="display:none">He who speak with forked tongue...may not necessarily be wise (or some such)...<br />Fairly simple tome. Japanese urban youth culture. Barbie girl goes to techno club and meets bad boy with a forked snake tongue obtained through gradual body modification/mutilation (take your pick). She becomes fascinated and turned on, they fuck immediately; she becomes immersed in the tattoo and piercing/ body modification world; wants a snake tongue, too, yadda yadda. Kind of fascinating so far as a socio-cultural thing. One bristles at the tongue piercing and slicing descriptions. But one is always interested in learning what goes on out there. Should have this done very quickly; it's super short. This won some sort of prize. So far, not entirely sure why. The author is quite a bit hot looking, maybe that influenced the jury. But it reads smoothly with no roadblocks or excess baggage, and that is something I am appreciating more. If this pre-review contains several instances of political incorrectness, then...it does.<br /><br />p. 44 (best passage in the book so far):<br />"I didn't care if Ama was Amadeus. Shiba-san was a son of God, and I was the only unexceptional one among us. All I wanted was to be part of an underground world where the sun doesn't shine, there are no serenades, and the sound of children's laughter is never, ever heard."<br /><br />Not half bad. I was left a bit undernourished by the lack of any real sense of character or identity about the girl narrator, though. I like that it came to no definite conclusion. The girl has a kind of pointless jaded, outlook. There are huge spoilers in this that I cannot mention; let's just say that a certain impetus for her splitting her tongue is lost. There are ruminations about loss, about how to live, and about how little we know about people we lose. I'm sure I'm missing a lot of metaphorical content about self-identity and body modification and all that. The book didn't really make me want to think much about it, really. To say the least, the 19-year-old gal seems to lack purpose; the attainment of the forked tongue and the elaborate tattoo on her back serves as one, and the attendant pain suggests a sort of purposeful kind of sacrifice and ritual; makes her feel alive. She identifies herself as a masochist at the beginning of the story, but we're never sure if she really is one, wholeheartedly. She surrounds herself with two sensitive bad boys, a classic conceit of chick lit. She wonders if if one or both of them might kill her; she doesn't seem to mind the prospect, or seem bothered that one of them asks if he can fuck her corpse after he kills her. There's a crime tangent in the story; a run-in with a young Yakuza punk that portends danger; and an element of hiding out in the underground. I can't say too much about it; spoilers and all that. Anyway, a good little yarn, but kind of a glorified short story more than a novel of true gravitas, it seemed to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1497763976943702092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2959788695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2959788695" />
    <a title="Stacie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34895792-stacie"><img alt="Stacie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601266056p2/34895792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2959788695?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacie" href="/user/show/34895792-stacie">Stacie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525948896" href="/book/show/922712.Snakes_and_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2959788695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12660401339145787723">What the hell did I just read??<br/><br/>I was looking for dark, but DAMN, this shit is <b>dark</b>. This is one that you'll either love & devour with all consuming tenacity OR hate with every fiber in your being & curse the book gods for putting it in your hands. Luckily, I fall into the 'loved it' category. <br/><br/>Not gonna lie, this was a screwed up story. It seems like a basic set up at first: a woman meets a man that will forever change the course of her life, and not in a cute way. One thing leads to another and </span>
  <span id="freeText12660401339145787723" style="display:none">What the hell did I just read??<br /><br />I was looking for dark, but DAMN, this shit is <b>dark</b>. This is one that you'll either love &amp; devour with all consuming tenacity OR hate with every fiber in your being &amp; curse the book gods for putting it in your hands. Luckily, I fall into the 'loved it' category. <br /><br />Not gonna lie, this was a screwed up story. It seems like a basic set up at first: a woman meets a man that will forever change the course of her life, and not in a cute way. One thing leads to another and this young woman finds herself in a downward spiral into the dark dregs of society. She ends up playing games with dangerous and unstable men. What could possibly go wrong? Answer: everything and more. <br /><br />Every character was nonredeemable, with grotesque action after grotesque action. The plot throws together three of the most unlikable and creepily sociopathic characters you'd ever read about, and also gives off an odd mater-of-fact tone to the horrible deeds done. There's no remorse to be found for any of the messed up stuff happening. But <b>I'll be damned if I wasn't hooked on every single word of this book.</b> <br /><br />I think I've been craving some different types of stories recently, and this one was certainly different. I could not believe what I was reading, and was downright flabbergasted the entire time, but in the best way possible. There's a reason why <i>Snakes and Earrings</i> won a few Japanese literary awards and sold a million copies. Everything about the story is completely bonkers. It's captivating, thrilling, and will make you question the morality of mankind. <br /><br />All that being said, <i>Snakes and Earrings</i> is not for the faint of heart. Please keep in mind that the author graphically details body modification, intensely violent (yet still consensual) sex, torture, rape, murder, desecration of bodies, and the list goes on. Basically, don't read this if you're squeamish. If you can handle those darker topics, then by all means, jump right into the crazy (borderline edgelord) romp through the streets of Tokyo. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12660401339145787723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3752441305668351425">This book is fairly raunchy, which I don't have a problem with. Unfortunately, it's also poorly written, which I do have a problem with. Perhaps the New York Times finds this story of BDSM and body modification to be "powerful," but I was unimpressed, having seen it all before. The supreme irony is that this is a book with adult content written by and for young people. The author is an incredibly hot 20-year old from Japan ("the youngest author ever to win Japan's prestigious Akutagawa Prize"), </span>
  <span id="freeText3752441305668351425" style="display:none">This book is fairly raunchy, which I don't have a problem with. Unfortunately, it's also poorly written, which I do have a problem with. Perhaps the New York Times finds this story of BDSM and body modification to be "powerful," but I was unimpressed, having seen it all before. The supreme irony is that this is a book with adult content written by and for young people. The author is an incredibly hot 20-year old from Japan ("the youngest author ever to win Japan's prestigious Akutagawa Prize"), and the cynic in me wonders if this hotness has anything to do with her book's status as an "international bestseller." It gets even worse at the very end of this so-called novel when she introduces an element of mystery so obvious as to be offensively obvious. At just over 100 small pages, the only justification is that one could read this in a single sitting. But why would you in a world with William Faulkner and Dorothy Allison?</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1742831311?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Madman Reads &amp; Rocks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Madman Reads &amp; Rocks " href="/user/show/45393113-ryan-madman-reads-rocks">Ryan Madman Reads &amp; Rocks </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742831311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11885634336330447747">Snakes and Earrings by Hitomi Kanehara is an interesting read. It also happens to be an international bestseller.<br/><br/>Lui (short for Louis Vuitton) is a young naive girl with a very self centered outlook on life. One day she meets Ama (short for Amadeus), a tattooed wannabe punk who encourages her to get her tongue split like a snake's tongue. Why? There are many reasons but the only reason that matters to Lui is because it will look "cool." <br/><br/>She also ends up having a lot of aggressive sex with Ama an</span>
  <span id="freeText11885634336330447747" style="display:none">Snakes and Earrings by Hitomi Kanehara is an interesting read. It also happens to be an international bestseller.<br /><br />Lui (short for Louis Vuitton) is a young naive girl with a very self centered outlook on life. One day she meets Ama (short for Amadeus), a tattooed wannabe punk who encourages her to get her tongue split like a snake's tongue. Why? There are many reasons but the only reason that matters to Lui is because it will look "cool." <br /><br />She also ends up having a lot of aggressive sex with Ama and claims to care about him even when she starts cheating on him with a tattoo artist named Shiba-Sahn.<br /><br />I found Lui's overall attitude quite tiresome. Though, I couldn't help but wonder how much was lost in translation. Maybe the original Japanese version offers up a more well rounded protagonist.<br /><br />The ending was somewhat intriguing and jarring. Some might consider it slightly offensive.<br /><br />Overall I give Snakes and Earrings by Hitomi Kanehara 4 out of 5 stars! ⭐⭐⭐⭐</span>

<div id="review_2545861104" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2545861104" />
    <a title="Pickle Farmer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1257892-pickle-farmer"><img alt="Pickle Farmer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481845676p2/1257892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2545861104?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pickle Farmer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pickle Farmer" href="/user/show/1257892-pickle-farmer">Pickle Farmer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2545861104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5923235611710392107">Wow, this was nuts!! It was very short and super readable - good for these dark, dark times. It was also an interesting read considering the female character. What really makes the book is despite how kinky and weird it is (she becomes obsessed with tattoos and piercing, which are linked VERY clearly with sex), she's also very self-aware of the bizarro male characters she meets. "This guy, I thought, was bizarre." (11) Or when her punk, snake tongue boyfriend mumbles "Sorry I'm so scary-looking"</span>
  <span id="freeText5923235611710392107" style="display:none">Wow, this was nuts!! It was very short and super readable - good for these dark, dark times. It was also an interesting read considering the female character. What really makes the book is despite how kinky and weird it is (she becomes obsessed with tattoos and piercing, which are linked VERY clearly with sex), she's also very self-aware of the bizarro male characters she meets. "This guy, I thought, was bizarre." (11) Or when her punk, snake tongue boyfriend mumbles "Sorry I'm so scary-looking" and she and her friend burst out laughing. This is what really MAKES the book for me... the fact that she's not like suckered into being like "omg, these body modification guys are so cool and I love them!" She's wry and knows what she's getting into.<br /><br />Another big part of her character is NIHILISM and SADISM, thus surely making this a classic among gothic, punk teens:<br /><br /><i>"I really didn't want to live in this kind of universe. I wanted to live recklessly and leave nothing behind but ashes in this dark, dull world."</i> (43) <br /><br /><i>"All I wanted was to be part of an underground world where the sun doesn't shine, there are no love songs, and the sound of children's laughter is never, ever heard."</i> (44) (Ha!)<br /><br /><i>"I often like to think that if sunlight reached into everywhere on the entire planet, I'd find a way to turn myself into a shadow."</i> (49)<br /><br /><i>"If you ever decide you want to die, let me kill you," said Shiba-sann. I smiled and nodded. He smiled back at me and asked, "Can I fuck your dead body?" "I don't care what happens to my body after I'm dead," I said with a shrug... I mean, for me, I've got absolutely no interest in my body if my mind no longer lives in it. I couldn't care less if I was eaten by dogs."</i> (72) (My margin notes here say OMG)<br /><br /><i>"I wondered if changing myself like this could be considered an insult to God, or an act of pure ego. I thought of how I had no real possessions, no emotional ties, no hatred. And it made me feel that my tattoo, my forked tongue, my future were all empty of meaning as well."</i> (77)<br /><br /> It's not really glamorised, though - she's clearly an alcoholic, as the other characters observe.<br /><br />The theme of body-modification throughout is also interesting, and leads to an interesting discussion of whether certain modification (i.e., splitting the tongue in two) is "against God's will," as it actually changes the shape of the body. Foot-binding, tightening with a corset, neck-extension, or even braces... very interesting how body modification is a part of so many human cultures. I'm sure an anthropologist would be able to tell me more. I'm sure it connects somehow to the idea of transformation + transcendence... A VERY interesting part to me was the section describing her job as a "companion," where she had to "play the part of a pleasant, polite Japanese girl": "Anyway, once my tongue was properly split, I'd never be doing this kind of work again." (56) I'm sure there's a thesis in here somewhere of women "transforming" themselves into acceptable vs. non-acceptable roles for society.<br /><br />My favourite thing about this book was how much it made me laugh. My least favourite thing is that I am REALLY, REALLY TIRED of the THIN, DAMAGED WOMAN CHARACTER... I see it in my students' work, "The Vegetarian," "Normal People" (yes in the case of these two novels it's a 'key' element to the girl's character) ... but I am just tired of it!!!!!!!!!! YOU CAN BE CHUNKY AND DAMAGED, NO?<br /><br />Other quotes:<br /><br /><i>"The constant pain also made me irritable and made me wish that everybody would just die."</i> (79)<br /><br /><i>"Possession can be such a hassle, and yet we are still driven by the desire to possess people and things. Maybe it appeals to the masochist and sadist in every one of us. As for me, I knew that no matter what else, the dragon and Kirin on my back would always be with me. They'd never betray me and I would never betray them."</i> (79)<br /><br /><i>"My life and future were pitch-black, and I couldn't see anything at the end of the tunnel. It's not as if I'd been expecting great things for myself before, it's just that now I could imagine myself just turning up dead in a gutter somewhere and I didn't even have the energy to laugh it off."</i> (81)<br /><br /><i> "What does go through someone's mind when they kill someone anyway? Do they think about the future? The people they care about? Their life all the way up to that moment? And how could I even begin to guess? I was a person who could see no future for myself, a person who cared about no one. I couldn't even understand my own life, which was little more than a pastiche of drunken moments."</i> (85)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5923235611710392107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5961152466950843438">Yes, the book is not likely to become classic, it does not bear any strong meaning or something. For most people this is more than enough to hate it and that, I believe, is totally okay with me. <br/>For me, this little book simply describes the small world of this kind of people that I do not even know how to label, you know, the ones who are so much into body art and look kind of scary to the rest of the world. The main character, as confused as she was, was nothing more than a new member in this l</span>
  <span id="freeText5961152466950843438" style="display:none">Yes, the book is not likely to become classic, it does not bear any strong meaning or something. For most people this is more than enough to hate it and that, I believe, is totally okay with me. <br />For me, this little book simply describes the small world of this kind of people that I do not even know how to label, you know, the ones who are so much into body art and look kind of scary to the rest of the world. The main character, as confused as she was, was nothing more than a new member in this little society. When she does eventually become part of it thanks to Ama, she is surprised to find that she is already addicted to living like this without even realizing it. <br />It is not hard to tell that she is dead inside, we are never told how and why this happened, maybe this is the reason why most people would judge her actions so harshly. You know, in other stories when it comes to having an affair, it becomes the centre of the heroine's thoughts, it is often even the whole point of the story. But not in this one - Lui hardly ever thinks about it, she never considers it a mistake.She is so broken that she does not realize how inlove she actually is, so she is uncapable of appreciating Ama, and I think that his death's only point is that Lui finally understands her feelings, with Ama the last piece of her soul died. <br />To sum up, it is a small book describing how a broken girl makes body art a part of her life, I believe, to fill in the emptiness caused by God-Knows-What. In my life I have met a lot of people like this and although I have never truly understood them, I've always wanted to. Well, this book provided a valuable insight into a little piece of this world for me and it's message is that simply that the reason for making such changes of one's body are not always so beautiful as the colourful ink on one's skin.</span>

<div id="review_598085612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/598085612" />
    <a title="Bjorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19667916-bjorn"><img alt="Bjorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367928200p2/19667916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/598085612?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bjorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bjorn" href="/user/show/19667916-bjorn">Bjorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19667916-bjorn?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer598085612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13565495564658764123">Lui is 19 and sick of being a good girl all dressed in pink and kawaii. She moves in with a violent boyfriend full of tattoos and piercings, and when he suggests piercing her tongue, she goes with it. It's all good and well until he introduces her to his tattoo artist, who enjoys inflicting pain a little more than most people... not that Lui minds.<br/><br/>Kanehara was 19 when she wrote this, a short novella of just 80 pages of three people pulling each other down into co-dependancy, alcohol and consensu</span>
  <span id="freeText13565495564658764123" style="display:none">Lui is 19 and sick of being a good girl all dressed in pink and kawaii. She moves in with a violent boyfriend full of tattoos and piercings, and when he suggests piercing her tongue, she goes with it. It's all good and well until he introduces her to his tattoo artist, who enjoys inflicting pain a little more than most people... not that Lui minds.<br /><br />Kanehara was 19 when she wrote this, a short novella of just 80 pages of three people pulling each other down into co-dependancy, alcohol and consensual violence, and it shows. Not that it's bad, absolutely not; much like Ryu Murakami's brilliant Almost Transparent Blue (Murakami wrote the foreword to this book too), it's a story of young people cut off from all accepted roles in Japanese society and responding by seeking pleasure in self-destruction, but where Murakami's story echoes on lots of different levels, Kanehara deliberately refuses to delve beneath the surface (fittingly for a book about people who change their skin to reflect how empty they feel on the inside). Lui is a frighteningly blank narrator; everything that happens to her, including her lover asking her if he can kill her, is dismissed with "that's OK." By limiting the story to what the emotionally dead Lui can be bothered to tell us, we end up with a story where almost every single thing that happens is related in the same bored monotone with no justification of why anybody does anything, forcing the reader to ask - if they care - just why these people act the way they do. If you find it genuinely affecting and thought-provoking, or just gratuitous shock value, will probably be different for each reader. I find myself somewhere in the middle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13565495564658764123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_296345180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/296345180" />
    <a title="randy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/959233-randy"><img alt="randy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1213230592p2/959233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/296345180?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="randy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="randy" href="/user/show/959233-randy">randy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer296345180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15887399926169427932">This book was free and only 120 pages. <br/>I figured it would be worth a read as the cover clearly states it won the Japanese award for best new literary talent.<br/><br/>Um... Not so much.<br/><br/>It took less than two hours to read, but I feel that every second I spent reading this I wasted and now have to live with the idea that I will never get them back. <br/><br/>First, this book seems only about titillation. And I am for good titillation as the next person, but this is far from the good kind. This is nihilist desperate t</span>
  <span id="freeText15887399926169427932" style="display:none">This book was free and only 120 pages. <br />I figured it would be worth a read as the cover clearly states it won the Japanese award for best new literary talent.<br /><br />Um... Not so much.<br /><br />It took less than two hours to read, but I feel that every second I spent reading this I wasted and now have to live with the idea that I will never get them back. <br /><br />First, this book seems only about titillation. And I am for good titillation as the next person, but this is far from the good kind. This is nihilist desperate titillation, where feeling is entirely absent.<br /><br />I can only assume that the translation of this story removed enormous amounts of underlying meaning. Well at least I hope that, or 2004 must have been a fallow year for Japanese fiction for this to win anything.<br /><br />Avoid, unless detachment in every way, minus retinal, is your idea of a good time. </span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8609664473438515217" style="display:none">"Know what a forked tongue is?"<br /> "One that's split in two?"<br /> "Yeah, like the tongue of a tongue of a snake or lizard. Except sometimes... they don't belong to a snake, and they don't belong to a lizard."<br /> He deliberately removed the cigarette from his lips and stuck out his tongue. Its tip was clearly split in two, just like that of a snake. Then i watched, transfixed, as he lifted the right tip of it, then skillfully grasped his cigarette in the crux of the "V."<br /> "Whoa..."<br /> This was my first encounter with a forked tongue. "Why don't you give it a try too?" he said. <br /> And without thought, by instinct alone, I nodded. <br /> Getting a forked tongue is normally something done by crazy people. They call it "body modification." But that didn't stop me from listening intently as he explained how it was done. Apparently you begin by getting your tongue pierced. You then gradually enlarge the hole by inserting bigger and bigger tongue rings. Then, when the hole has been stretched to a certain size, you tie dental floss or finishing line tight loops running from the hole down the middle of the tongue. Finally, you cut the remaining part of the tongue that's still connected using either a scalpel or a razor blade. In fact, some people don't even bother going through the whole pierce-and-tie process at all - they just slice their tongue in two with a scalpel...<br /><br />So starts one of the most vivid and believable novellas i have ever written. Intriguing, huh? Well this story will rivet you and involve you so effectively, that even after you're done reading, you will still be so overwhelmed by your sympathetic feelings for the characters, and you will not soon forget. Reading it was like watching a really good drama movie. Monika, if you are reading this review, it is for you: i think you will really like this book.<br /><br />P.S. seems like people didn't like the translated version? I can see it already actually, from just transcribing the introduction of the English translated version from Amazon.com...</span>

<div id="review_2766367415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2766367415" />
    <a title="Hanifa Yasmeen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57145639-hanifa-yasmeen"><img alt="Hanifa Yasmeen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555000765p2/57145639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2766367415?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hanifa Yasmeen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hanifa Yasmeen" href="/user/show/57145639-hanifa-yasmeen">Hanifa Yasmeen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2766367415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14210389922735386065">I want to give this book a lower rating than 3 but higher than 2, so let's just say 2.5. I liked that this book was short and so I could read it in one sitting; any more than that and I would consider it a complete waste of my time. I'm not sure if I'm not the right audience of this book or if it was too deep for me to 'get it' but I failed to resonate with any character or scene. It borderline romanticized anorexia, depression and dependence, which for obvious reasons is problematic; plus the c</span>
  <span id="freeText14210389922735386065" style="display:none">I want to give this book a lower rating than 3 but higher than 2, so let's just say 2.5. I liked that this book was short and so I could read it in one sitting; any more than that and I would consider it a complete waste of my time. I'm not sure if I'm not the right audience of this book or if it was too deep for me to 'get it' but I failed to resonate with any character or scene. It borderline romanticized anorexia, depression and dependence, which for obvious reasons is problematic; plus the characters are TEENAGERS like????? Please stop, no. Such overly graphic sexual presentation and sadistic depiction of a minor is not necessary in today's literature. We can honestly do better. <br /><br />The central character, Lui identifies herself as a masochist and her identity is not really explored beyond that. The characters are really flat and their whole personality is defined by 2-3 characteristics, which puts them in a box; pretty black and white. I did like the comparison of body modification and enhancement to being God as possession of power to change and make things according to your will, to create an image that you have control over yourself and you are not subservient to a higher power but the main character seems to fail to exercise her free will, fail to create her own path and make decisions and is very passive about her own life. In fact, the only power she has over herself is with deciding her piercings and tattoos. A good dialogue for a better take on the story was created but it failed to take it any further. The whole body modification part also gave a nod towards self-identity and dysphoria, that part was portrayed well. <br /><br />But overall, I do not agree with the romanticizing of deliberate pain as some kind of ritual and dependence and surrender of young age. The problems that this book brings up to the surface and recognizes, it fails to provide a handle over, a space for discourse, a way out of it but instead further adds to the problem of the many, many stories on mental health present today.<br /><br />TL; DR: The book is problematic, not really worth a read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14210389922735386065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384752850?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carola" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carola" href="/user/show/5152053-carola">Carola</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099483670" href="/book/show/922711.Snakes_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=has-review">has-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=japanese-literature">japanese-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=selling">selling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152053-carola?shelf=ubl">ubl</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384752850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15030655934074127755">Let me begin by being frank: for me, this book was a whole load of 'meh'.<br/><br/>First of all, I wasn't impressed by the plot. The plot twist wasn't a real plot twist – could have seen it coming from a mile away – and there’s no mystery about the plot either. We don’t get a real resolution by the end but you still know what happened around the time it first starts happening. (Sorry, while I don’t think there’s much to spoil about this book, I’ll still try to avoid spoilers).<br/><br/>I don’t think you are suppose</span>
  <span id="freeText15030655934074127755" style="display:none">Let me begin by being frank: for me, this book was a whole load of 'meh'.<br /><br />First of all, I wasn't impressed by the plot. The plot twist wasn't a real plot twist – could have seen it coming from a mile away – and there’s no mystery about the plot either. We don’t get a real resolution by the end but you still know what happened around the time it first starts happening. (Sorry, while I don’t think there’s much to spoil about this book, I’ll still try to avoid spoilers).<br /><br />I don’t think you are supposed to like anything about this book. An approach that works for some books but left me unimpressed with this one. To me, the characters are wholly unlikeable and so were their relationships. Nothing that happens in the plot is in any way likeable. And I imagine the book’s intention is to shock (but correct me if I'm wrong) and for me it didn't even achieve that. All this talk about piercings and tattoos just doesn't work on me (as in: it simply doesn't shock me).<br /><br />Maybe I'm not the intended audience? Although I'm not sure who this book is supposed to be for. Young adults, supposedly? I can imagine this book is interesting to a certain audience, I just can’t quite pinpoint what audience that would be. It’s a short book, so it doesn't hurt to give it a try (but you’re also not missing out if you don’t read it). I know I sound unreasonably negative, but believe me, I didn't hate it and I don’t regret reading it.<br /><br />The book won both the Subaru Literary Prize and the prestigious Akutagawa Prize, the latter being judged by acclaimed novelist <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8881.Ry__Murakami" title="Ryū Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Ryū Murakami</a>. I haven’t read enough by Ryū Murakami (only <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17810.In_the_Miso_Soup" title="In the Miso Soup by Ryū Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Miso Soup</a>, which I thought was alright), but from what I know, I imagine if you like his novels, you might also enjoy <i>Snakes &amp; Earrings</i>. Somewhat tamer, for a (supposedly) YA audience.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15030655934074127755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_41264285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41264285" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1843426-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41264285?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/1843426-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843426-danielle?shelf=assigned-reading">assigned-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843426-danielle?shelf=relates-to-japan">relates-to-japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1843426-danielle?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41264285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17755302997715793835">If you can't handle sadism and masochism, please avoid this book. It is explicit in its descriptions of sex and mutilation, so it certainly is not for everyone. Read it if these subjects don't bother you and you are interested in learning about a niche of subculture that has gained media attention in recent years. It's quite short - should only take you a couple of hours, tops.<br/><br/>I liked the empty tone of the work and the seeming nonchalance of the main character that surfaced at times. That said, </span>
  <span id="freeText17755302997715793835" style="display:none">If you can't handle sadism and masochism, please avoid this book. It is explicit in its descriptions of sex and mutilation, so it certainly is not for everyone. Read it if these subjects don't bother you and you are interested in learning about a niche of subculture that has gained media attention in recent years. It's quite short - should only take you a couple of hours, tops.<br /><br />I liked the empty tone of the work and the seeming nonchalance of the main character that surfaced at times. That said, this isn't anything particularly profound or even original - I have no idea why it won the Aktagawa award in Japan... it's not great literature. Don't believe most of the reviews - I don't think it's any sort of "portrait of the post-bubble Japan." It's a plausible book, despite its extremism, but it's not typical of most Japanese situations, as far as I know, and so is far from "portrait" material. Hmm, I should say that its emptiness may be very "post-bubble" as far as that goes, but other books address that better, so that this really can't be considered a good example of the theme or as representative of the era/situation.<br /><br />Just my two cents, anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17755302997715793835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
