<div id="review_621032604" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621032604" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386476-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332711164p2/8386476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621032604?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/8386476-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099483670" href="/book/show/922711.Snakes_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386476-alex?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621032604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3102604541697938305">Read 21/05/2013<br/><br/>Nicely written, and a somewhat interesting story. I think that on the surface it appears quite easy to understand, but there's probably more to think about, and it feels like the sort of book I want to read more about, and have discussions about. There must be some reasoning behind Lui's actions, why she gets sucked into this world, why she chooses to follow Ama's body modification trail. <br/><br/>I can't help but feel the book was too short for the story. The first 70 pages or so all felt</span>
  <span id="freeText3102604541697938305" style="display:none">Read 21/05/2013<br /><br />Nicely written, and a somewhat interesting story. I think that on the surface it appears quite easy to understand, but there's probably more to think about, and it feels like the sort of book I want to read more about, and have discussions about. There must be some reasoning behind Lui's actions, why she gets sucked into this world, why she chooses to follow Ama's body modification trail. <br /><br />I can't help but feel the book was too short for the story. The first 70 pages or so all felt quite nicely paced, but then it felt like at the end a huge chunk of development was left out in order to round the story off within a short number of pages.<br /><br />This also caused a few problems with the development and connection to the characters - none were fully introduced, no details were ever truly exchanged about any of them. It felt like a group of unknown characters, ad maybe that's the point - in order to shine more light onto the themes of the book, rather than getting weighed down with who these people are. <br /><br />As it is, I did enjoy reading the book very much, but it's also one that I think I'd like to read again - which I guess is the sign of a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3102604541697938305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikita" href="/user/show/3103148-nikita">Nikita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525948896" href="/book/show/922712.Snakes_and_Earrings">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nikita by: </span>
      Amie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3103148-nikita?shelf=no-sir">no-sir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88434306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2062836353949357665">Let me say this first - Snakes and Earrings by Hitomi Kanechara is short. 120, largish text, double-spaced short. It is also reasonably engrossing read - I picked it up around midnight last night and finished it by 1:30. However, this book didn't leave me with much of anything. Our 'heroine' Lui is complacent and one-dimensional, her boyfriend Ama and part-time lover Shiba-san are not much better, and the reader is left with the sense that the body modification and surrounding culture that this </span>
  <span id="freeText2062836353949357665" style="display:none">Let me say this first - Snakes and Earrings by Hitomi Kanechara is short. 120, largish text, double-spaced short. It is also reasonably engrossing read - I picked it up around midnight last night and finished it by 1:30. However, this book didn't leave me with much of anything. Our 'heroine' Lui is complacent and one-dimensional, her boyfriend Ama and part-time lover Shiba-san are not much better, and the reader is left with the sense that the body modification and surrounding culture that this book explores is really supposed to <i>mean</i> something, but the whole novel for me was just lost in translation. The words are empty, and don't even have the courtesy to be pretty. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2062836353949357665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FaoRAEffHVjChR98VHiKABjP6/uVA8ZXnK755Nq4725XCKMyRXzsIhBjM4dLpEq2qjbMELtZbM7ho+Ac9gpykQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2cm3vvuA+cDJvTa9UQIuoYNEExrYh6IRM36irqld9E+bawWM+SMIuhtbGkZO3u4XMb008fbdCIhOc7tWhe9psA==')})
  }

Ryu Murakami\'s first novel, Almost Transparent Blue won the coveted Akutagawa literary prize and became an instant bestseller. Representing a sharp and conscious turning away from the introspective trend of postwar Japanese literature, it polarized critics and public alike and soon attracted international attention as an At the outset, the young men seem louche but harmless, their activities limited to drinking, snacking, peering at a naked neighbor through a window, and performing karaoke. The six &quot;aunties&quot; are fiercely independent career women. When one of the boys executes a lethal ambush of one of the women, chaos ensues. The women band together to find the killer and exact revenge. In turn, the boys buckle down, study physics, and plot to take out their nemeses in a single blast. Who knew that a deadly &quot;gang war&quot; could be such fun? The first novel <i>Snakes and Earings</i> won the Akutagawa Prize and the Subaru Prize and it sold a million copies.</span>
